## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form of (forced/damped) nonlinear oscillators in classical mechanics. Common models include linear harmonic motion plus nonlinear stiffness, nonlinear damping, and external/parametric forcing terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped, unforced): dv_dt = -c0 * x (Hooke restoring acceleration)
- Linear damping oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- General time-dependent forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + f(t), e.g., f(t) = c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (arbitrary drive encoded as trig in t)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Softening spring with quintic correction: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (higher-order stiffness nonlinearity)
- Pendulum (exact, no small-angle): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v (angle x; nonlinear restoring torque)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (self-excited oscillations via negative damping at small |x|)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (self-excitation via nonlinear damping in v)
- Quadratic drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like damping proportional to v|v|)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * sign(v) (stick-slip-like velocity sign dissipation; sign approximations often used in regression)
- Nonlinear mixed damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x**2 * v (amplitude-dependent dissipation)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-periodic stiffness modulation)
- Time-varying damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * v (periodic or scheduled damping changes)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope Ôćĺ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects Ôćĺ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay Ôćĺ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior Ôćĺ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects Ôćĺ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: odd-in-x terms (x, x**3, sin(x)) typically indicate conservative symmetric potentials; even-in-x terms suggest asymmetry or bias.
- Conservative vs dissipative split: terms depending only on x (or sin(x)) act like potential forces; terms proportional to v, v*Abs(v), sign(v), or v**3 indicate dissipation/energy injection.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency shift: inclusion of x**3, x**5, or sin(x) often produces frequency that varies with oscillation amplitude (non-isochronous behavior).
- Self-excited limit cycles: factors like (c0 - c1 * x**2) * v or (c0 - c1 * v**2) * v encode negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, yielding stable oscillations.
- Dry friction signatures: near piecewise behavior in v (sign(v) or v/(Abs(v)+c)) implies stick-slip and non-smooth dynamics, often seen as sharp corners in phase portraits.
- Aerodynamic/impact-like dissipation: v*Abs(v) (or higher odd powers in v) indicates drag increasing with speed, causing faster decay at high velocities than near equilibrium.
- Periodic driving/parametric effects: explicit sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms (either additive forcing or multiplicative with x) indicate resonance phenomena and possible instability tongues (parametric resonance).
- State coupling hints: terms like x**2 * v or x * v encode damping or forcing that depends on amplitude/phase, often used to model nonlinear friction or energy transfer mechanisms.

- `-1.29395390256765*x**3` Ôćĺ cubic in x
- `-1.29395390256765*x*(0.0943056786339846*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1)` Ôćĺ this expands to `-1.29395390256765*0.0943056786339846*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) - 1.29395390256765*x`

**x*|v|^(1/3)** cannot be represented by `v*x`, `v┬▓*|x|`, `v*|x|`, `x┬▓*v`, or polynomial terms.

Let me scan all 50 candidates for the presence of `sin(v)` or any function that could produce it:

None of the candidates contain `sin(v)` or any trigonometric function. They all use polynomials, exponentials, logarithms, and absolute values.

Since `sin(v)` is linearly independent from all polynomial, exponential, and logarithmic basis functions, and the coefficient of `sin(v)` in the GT is `-0.448...` (non-zero), **no candidate can match the GT**.

Even if we could somehow approximate `sin(v)` with a polynomial (which we CANNOT per Rule 2 - no approximations), the `x*|v|^(1/3)` term would still be missing.
